"},{"Title":"Comment on how the dramatic and cinematic elements bring out the literary elements- RRM","Date":"25 April 2004","Score":"0 out of 2 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Comedy, Drama, Romance","Review":"  Harold and Maude was a funny, yet somewhat strange movie.  The topic of the movie is not something you usually hear about and it is something you probably would not think of.  This is truely a unique movie.As I watched this movie, I found that the director used many dramatic and cinematic elements to reveal the literary elements, as do other directors. In this comment, I will list and give my thoughts on a few of these.I will begin with one of the more effective techniques.  Throughout the film, the director used many edits to show the feelings and thought of a character, revealing who they really were.  As something was going on, the director would change the camera position or angle to show a close up of a character.  Through the facial expressions, you could tell how the character felt about the subject being discussed.  I found this particularly effective when Harold's mother would lecture Harold, showing Harold's expressions as she talked.Another effective technique would be the longshots the director chose to use to reveal the setting.  Two in particular stuck in my head. They were the cemetary scene and the cliff scene.  The Cemetary scene was amazing because it was so huge.  The camera continuously Zoomed out, creating a bigger cemetary.  The cliff scene was also pretty neat, starting with the car and Zooming out revealing how large the cliff was and also revealing that Herald was steal alive.  The Director also effectively used medium shots, especially when Herald visits the few men about his relationship with Maude. The shot was zoomed out far enough, showing their desk and things hanging on the wall, so that we could tell who they were or what they were by looking on the desk or wall.I also found the parrellel editing towards the end pretty neat.  At the same time, the director revealed what was happening in the hospital and what was happening afterwards, revealing the plot in a different, but effective way. Most people think of Harold and Maude as a cult classic; as a funny, offbeat, and one of the most interesting dark comedies every made. Well, I'd most certainly agree with interesting (in terms of how nothing in it was to be expected), but I would substitute funny and offbeat with appalling and off-putting with only a handful of humorous moments.The plot is absolutely preposterous and not one that really intrigued me to begin with. Bud Cort stars in the film as a young, death-obsessed man still living with his mother. He is so obsessed with dying and scaring people that he's attempted to scare his mother and other people by faking his own suicide with a variety of unimaginative methods. Then he comes upon and falls in love with a seventy-nine-year-old woman whose just as obsessed with life as he is with death. And together, they embark on a series of wild and eventually romantic adventures.Weird! Now the plot of the movie itself is very off-putting and let me warn you that the content that follows especially within the last third of the movie is most certainly wrongheaded and disturbing in a bad way. For the first two-thirds, I was not enormously entertained, I probably still wouldn't have recommended the movie, but I wasn't appalled. Then in that third act, it goes so over the top, so self-incriminating, and ultimately the movie shoots it's already-weak self in the foot and falls like a ton of bricks. The third act my itself destroyed the movie for me because it was completely creepy to me. And in the worst way possible. Now, I am not against being creeped or grossed out in a movie, but it has to be done right. I still consider The Silence of the Lambs (1991) as the creepiest movie I've ever seen and graphically, it's more disturbing than Harold and Maude, but the content of The Silence of the Lambs is, strangely, off-putting in a fantastic way. How it's treated here in Harold and Maude is wrong in literally every sense, it's disturbing, and left me eager for the credits to roll and overjoyed when at last they finally did appear.Now Harold and Maude is not a COMPLETE disaster for me, but it's only a hair's length away from being one. It's saved from being a catastrophe and ends up just being mediocre because there were three genuinely humorous moments in the film that were not off-putting, not creepy in a bad sense, and were imaginative and welcome. Alonzo for the noir look of the movie.But still, in the end, Harold and Maude proved to be nothing to me but a grim, disturbing, and eventually and appalling excuse for a romantic comedy that I also fear will offend a great many people over a broad variety for various reasons. These elements often help bring out the literary elements of the film including plot, character development, and emotional connections. Most of the elements are cinematic, but there are many examples of dramatic elements as well. In the opening scene, there are several examples of dramatic elements including the patchy lighting on the staircase, light and happy music, candles being lit, and he even writes a letter.  These things open the story with a contradictory mood.  The patchy lighting brings a dark mood, but the music has a lighter mood.  The mix is confusing, but the mood is severely altered to a depressing mood when he hangs himself.  Although, the mood quickly changes back when his mother walks in and completely ignores the fact that he hangs there.  The movie is full of these confusing mood swings, but the viewer gets used to the fact that this is not a normal story. There are many cinematic elements that bring out the literary elements of the story.  For example, there are several different shots taken that contain no dialogue, and the viewer only sees a scene with music.  When Harold gets his new Jaguar, a shot is taken of him welding something.  The viewer cannot see what he is welding, but this shot foreshadows a change in something metal.  The conclusion that he is changing his car is made by the viewer during this scene, and it is confirmed later on when his new sports hearse is revealed.  Another shot is taken of Harold and Maude dancing. This shot shows the connection growing between the two.  This one single shot develops both of the characters and shows that Harold is changing. One scene was taken of Harold playing the banjo which deepens the viewer's understanding that Harold is changing into a happy person because of love. The action scenes, especially the ones with the motorcycle cop, really dig deep into the characters and show more of their new-found connection. There are a lot of other examples of how the cinematic and dramatic elements in this film help to bring out the literary elements.  Irony is used a lot in this film, and the speech and actions of the characters, especially Harold, help show it.  These elements may or may not create a good movie, but they do create an interesting story.
